# How to Encourage Jira Hygiene Without Creating Friction | Hivel

chevron-right**One Pager Sprint Hygiene Checklist**[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#one-pager-sprint-hygiene-checklist)

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#before-starting-every-sprint)

Before Starting Every Sprint

☐ All tickets in the sprint have story points ☐ All tickets are linked to an Epic ☐ All tickets have a single assignee ☐ Sprint scope has team agreement before clicking Start Sprint

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#during-the-sprint)

During the Sprint

☐ Avoid adding new tickets unless work is urgent or blocking ☐ Any ticket added mid-sprint is clearly marked as unplanned ☐ If new work is added, discuss scope tradeoffs in standups ☐ Update story points only if scope or complexity truly changes

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#before-moving-tickets-to-done)

Before Moving Tickets to Done

☐ Work fully meets the team’s Definition of Done ☐ No open subtasks remain ☐ Required fields such as resolution are set ☐ Done reflects real completion, not just code finished

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#before-closing-the-sprint)

Before Closing the Sprint

☐ All completed tickets are in Done ☐ Incomplete tickets are moved to the next sprint and re-estimated if needed ☐ Done tickets are not carried forward ☐ Sprint is closed on time without extending dates

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#recommended-low-effort-automations)

Recommended Low-Effort Automations

☐ Flag tickets added after sprint start as unplanned ☐ Block Done if required fields or subtasks are incomplete ☐ Auto-set resolution when issues move to Done ☐ Warn when issues enter a sprint without story points or Epic

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#board-visibility-checks)

Board Visibility Checks

☐ Quick filter for tickets missing story points ☐ Quick filter for tickets without Epics ☐ Separate visibility for unplanned work ☐ Dashboards shared with the team, not just managers

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#key-principle-to-remember)

Key Principle to Remember

Jira hygiene should be **automatic, visible, and enforced at key moments**. If it relies on reminders or manual policing, it will not scale.

Effective Jira hygiene is not about enforcing discipline through reminders. It is about configuring Jira so that clean data is the default outcome.

The steps below are ordered by **impact vs effort**.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#id-1.-enforce-hygiene-at-sprint-boundaries)

1\. Enforce Hygiene at Sprint Boundaries

Sprint boundaries are the single most important control point.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#what-to-enforce)

What to enforce

Before starting a sprint, ensure that:

*   All work items in the sprint have story points
    
*   All work items are linked to an Epic
    
*   All work items have an assignee
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#how-to-implement)

How to implement

Option A. Sprint checklist approach

*   During sprint planning, filter the backlog by “Missing story points” and “No Epic”
    
*   Resolve these in bulk before clicking Start Sprint
    

**Option B. Automation approach (recommended)**

*   Create a Jira Automation rule that triggers when a sprint starts
    
*   Condition: work items in sprint missing required fields
    
*   Action: comment on those work items or notify the sprint owner
    

**Reference** Atlassian sprint planning best practices [https://www.atlassian.com/agile/scrum/sprint-planningarrow-up-right](https://www.atlassian.com/agile/scrum/sprint-planning)

**Why this works** It prevents dirty data from entering the sprint without interrupting daily execution.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#id-2.-require-fields-only-when-they-become-relevant)

2\. Require Fields Only When They Become Relevant

One of the biggest sources of friction is making fields mandatory too early.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#recommended-pattern)

Recommended pattern

*   Story points required only when an issue moves into an active sprint
    
*   Assignee required only when work starts
    
*   Epic required for stories and tasks, not necessarily for bugs
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#how-to-implement-1)

How to implement

*   Use workflow validators on status transitions
    
*   Apply field requirements on “To Do → In Progress” or “Backlog → Sprint”
    

**Reference** Jira workflow conditions and validators

[https://support.atlassian.com/jira-cloud-administration/docs/configure-advanced-issue-workflows/arrow-up-right](https://support.atlassian.com/jira-cloud-administration/docs/configure-advanced-issue-workflows/)

**Why this works** Contextual enforcement feels helpful instead of bureaucratic.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#id-3.-automate-what-humans-should-not-have-to-remember)

3\. Automate What Humans Should Not Have to Remember

Automation should handle repetitive hygiene checks silently.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#high-impact-automations-to-set-up)

High-impact automations to set up

1.  Flag unplanned work automatically
    

*   Trigger: issue added to an active sprint
    
*   Action: add label “unplanned” or comment explaining it was added mid-sprint
    

1.  Auto-set resolution on Done
    

*   Trigger: issue transitions to Done
    
*   Action: set resolution field
    

1.  Warn on missing estimates or ownership
    

*   Trigger: issue moved to In Progress
    
*   Condition: missing story points or assignee
    
*   Action: comment or notify
    

**Reference** Jira Automation rule library

[https://support.atlassian.com/cloud-automation/docs/jira-cloud-automation/arrow-up-right](https://support.atlassian.com/cloud-automation/docs/jira-cloud-automation/)

**Why this works** Automation enforces consistency without social friction.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#id-4.-encode-definition-of-done-in-the-workflow)

4\. Encode Definition of Done in the Workflow

Documentation alone does not enforce behavior.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#what-to-enforce-in-jira)

What to enforce in Jira

*   Prevent work items from moving to Done if:
    
    *   Required fields are missing
        
    *   Open subtasks still exist
        
    *   QA or review steps are incomplete
        
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#how-to-implement-2)

How to implement

*   Add workflow validators on the Done transition
    
*   Optionally auto-transition subtasks when the parent issue is completed
    

**Reference** Defining and enforcing Done in Jira

[https://www.atlassian.com/blog/jira/8-steps-to-a-definition-of-done-in-jiraarrow-up-right](https://www.atlassian.com/blog/jira/8-steps-to-a-definition-of-done-in-jira)

**Why this works** It ensures Done reflects real completion and keeps reports trustworthy.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#id-5.-use-visibility-instead-of-hard-blocks-where-possible)

5\. Use Visibility Instead of Hard Blocks Where Possible

Not every hygiene issue needs to be blocked.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#recommended-visibility-patterns)

Recommended visibility patterns

*   Board quick filters for “Missing story points”
    
*   Dashboard gadget for “Work items without Epics”
    
*   Separate swimlane or filter for unplanned work
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#how-to-implement-3)

How to implement

*   Leverage Hivel's dashboards for the above.
    

**Why this works** Teams naturally correct what they can see without being forced.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#id-6.-treat-sprint-start-and-end-dates-as-sacred)

6\. Treat Sprint Start and End Dates as Sacred

Sprint dates directly affect velocity and reporting.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#best-practices)

Best practices

*   Do not start sprints retroactively
    
*   Do not extend sprints to “finish” work
    
*   Close sprints on time even if work remains
    

**Reference** How Jira calculates velocity and sprint reports [https://support.atlassian.com/jira-software-cloud/docs/view-and-understand-the-velocity-chart/arrow-up-right](https://support.atlassian.com/jira-software-cloud/docs/view-and-understand-the-velocity-chart/)

**Why this works** Accurate dates preserve long-term trend reliability.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#id-7.-clarify-story-points-vs-subtasks)

7\. Clarify Story Points vs Subtasks

This prevents a very common reporting issue.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#guidance)

Guidance

*   Story points should live on the parent issue
    
*   Subtasks are for execution breakdown only
    
*   Avoid estimating subtasks unless you fully understand the reporting impact
    

**Why this works** Velocity and sprint reports rely on parent work items, not subtasks.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/best-practices/jira-best-practices/how-to-encourage-jira-hygiene-without-creating-friction#key-takeaway)

Key Takeaway

Jira hygiene works when:

*   Rules are enforced only at key moments
    
*   Automation replaces reminders
    
*   Visibility replaces micromanagement
    
*   Workflow gates protect data integrity
    

If hygiene depends on people remembering rules, it will fail. If hygiene is encoded into Jira’s structure, it sustains itself.

* * *

# Alerts in Hivel | Hivel

Alerts let you know when important engineering metrics cross the thresholds you care about, so you don’t have to constantly check dashboards.

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel#why-alerts-matter)

Why Alerts Matter


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel#for-executives-cto-vp-of-engineering)

For Executives (CTO, VP of Engineering)

*   Get signals when org-wide delivery metrics move out of healthy ranges (like Cycle Time, MTTR, Release Merge Frequency, Change Failure Rate, etc.)
    
*   Stay ahead of reliability issues without digging across dashboards
    
*   Keep a steady pulse on team performance across the org
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel#for-engineering-managers-team-leads)

For Engineering Managers/Team Leads

*   Catch slowdowns early (for example: Cycle Time > 5 days)
    
*   Monitor team-wide patterns before sprint planning or reviews
    
*   Maintain alignment with expectations and avoid last-minute surprises
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel#for-developers)

For Developers

*   Get nudges when your PRs wait too long for review
    
*   Monitor personal patterns like coding time, review time, or PR activity
    
*   Stay aware of your own trends without manually checking dashboards
    

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel#alert-types-scopes)

Alert Types (Scopes)


---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Hivel supports three alert scopes. Each scope controls what the alert monitors:

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel#id-1.-organization-level-alerts)

1\. Organization-Level Alerts

*   Watch metrics across the entire org
    
*   Great for executives or central engineering operations
    
*   Only admins / execs with “complete data visibility” can configure them
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel#id-2.-team-level-alerts)

2\. Team-Level Alerts

*   Monitor metrics for a single team
    
*   Ideal for managers responsible for specific groups
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel#id-3.-personal-alerts)

3\. Personal Alerts

*   Users can set alerts for themselves or any other individual, on teams they choose
    
*   Great for PR reminders or personal productivity patterns
    

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel#before-you-start-permissions)

Before You Start - Permissions


-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Make sure your role is assigned the correct permissions in the [Access Managementarrow-up-right](https://app.hivel.ai/settings/rbac)
 screen:

*   **Modify Alerts** – Create/edit/delete alerts (Org & Team level)
    
*   **View Alerts Menu** – Access the alert dashboard
    
*   **Modify Alerts Config** – Configure Slack channels & digests (Org & Team level only)
    
*   **Personal Alerts** – Create/edit personal alerts regardless of access to above permissions
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FhyWfMtJLyVe9FiUA7tIq%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D4b3cf31a-b1c2-4dc7-912b-de1a7ddfd044&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=325cb27b&sv=2)

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel#how-to-set-up-an-alert-step-by-step)

How to Set Up an Alert (Step-by-Step)


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Navigate to **Alerts** under **Overview**, choose the scope you want, and click on "New Alert".

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FnYbAE8NTZTCH8wHjiKHQ%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd21fc426-908b-4a6b-86ae-588501ff9500&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c99318c9&sv=2)

Here is a short walkthrough of the Alerts setup process:

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252F5nwRFlROh4hA0CAVexnH%252FScreen%2520Recording%25202025-12-10%2520at%252011.27.03%25E2%2580%25AFAM.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D30df114d-81f0-4795-a869-d1c6a7114e81&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=8c3e16e6&sv=2)

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel#id-1.-choose-your-metric-and-set-the-threshold)

1\. Choose your metric & set the threshold

Note:

*   A metric can only have one alert per scope _(Example: only one Cycle Time alert allowed at the org level)_
    
*   Metrics already used at that level won’t appear in the dropdown
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel#id-2.-choose-when-the-alert-should-fire)

2\. Choose when the alert should fire

Hivel uses time-window averages, not real-time checks, to avoid spam.

You can either:

*   Use an existing Digest schedule
    
*   Or set a Custom schedule for just this alert (daily, weekly, or monthly)
    

> Note: If you choose a date above 28 for a monthly alert, the system will warn you that alerts won’t fire for the months that don’t have those dates.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel#id-3.-select-recipients)

3\. Select recipients

You can send alerts to:

*   Slack
    
*   Email
    
*   Or both
    

> **Note:** For Slack, make sure you've integrated it with Hivel and set up the Slack channels ([details in this guidearrow-up-right](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel/setting-up-slack-to-receive-hivel-alerts)
> ).

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel#id-4.-review-and-save)

4\. Review & save

Review the Alert settings and click Save. Your alert will now appear in the Alerts table.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel#creating-a-digest-optional)

Creating a Digest (Optional)

Digests help you group multiple alerts into a single scheduled summary to avoid notification overload.

To create one:

1.  Go to Alerts → Settings ⚙️ icon → Digests
    
2.  Create a digest with a name, timing, recipients, and Slack channel or emails.
    
    ![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FGR2F3tWi0r0ZNqPwPU2d%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D023a9877-f3f3-465f-ac56-23319283ec04&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=920e9c41&sv=2)
    
3.  Assign alerts to this digest during alert creation.
    

circle-info

**Note:** If a digest does not have any email recipients configured, you will not be able to add email addresses during alert creation. In this case, update the email recipients in the digest configuration first, and then proceed to create the alert.

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel#how-hivel-manages-alerts-behind-the-scenes)

How Hivel Manages Alerts Behind the Scenes


-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Only one alert per metric per scope is allowed.
    
*   Each scope (Org, Team, Personal) can have its own Slack channel.
    
*   If a digest is deleted, all linked alerts automatically switch to custom schedules using the digest’s original timing.
    
*   If a Slack channel is deleted, alerts using only Slack are disabled until a new channel is added.
    
*   If a team in an alert is deleted, the alert becomes inactive until updated.
    

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/alerts-in-hivel#need-help)

Need Help?


--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

If you’re unable to see Alert options or need assistance setting things up, reach us at [\[email protected\]](https://docs.hivel.ai/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection)
.

# How to archive users? | Hivel

Archiving users is essential when individuals leave the organization or when their data is no longer relevant.

Regularly doing this activity helps ensure that metrics remain accurate and free of unnecessary data.

To archive users, you can simply:

1.  Go the Setting screen -> Teams
    
2.  Select the particular users
    
3.  Click on Archive button in the top right
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FUt20UNkXUhjCXlielgFs%252FGIF%2520Recording%2520Aug%252022%2520from%2520Jumpshare.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D4560f275-55ad-463f-a85e-55fd6983022a&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=5974f2cc&sv=2)

To unarchive any user, please reach out to [\[email protected\]envelope](https://docs.hivel.ai/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#cdbeb8bdbda2bfb98da5a4bba8a1e3aca4)
.

# Team Versioning | Hivel

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/team-versioning#what-is-team-versioning)

What is Team Versioning?

**Team Versioning** provides the flexibility to view metrics based on **how teams were structured during the selected time period**, preserving historical accuracy.

By default, Hivel metrics reflect the current team structure - meaning that past metric values are calculated based on **today’s team structure**, not how the team was structured historically.

**With Team Versioning enabled:**

*   Historical data remains intact.
    
*   Team member additions, removals, and transfer dates are respected.
    
*   Metrics reflect who was actually part of the team during the selected date range.
    

This prevents productivity metrics from being retroactively distorted when team composition changes.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/team-versioning#default-behavior-without-team-versioning)

**🔍 Default Behavior (Without Team Versioning)**

*   Metrics are always calculated using the **current team structure**.
    
*   If an author moves teams, their past contributions are still shown under their **new team**, not where they were when the work was done.
    
*   Only current state data is visible.
    
*   Removing a team member from all the teams removes them from all views.
    
*   Historical contributions are not time-aware.
    

**Example:**

*   Author A was in Team B from Jan to Feb.
    
*   In March, Author A is moved to Team C.
    
*   You view Team B metrics from **Jan 15 – Feb 15**: 👉 Without Team Versioning, **Author A's contributions will not show** under Team B (since they are now in Team C).
    

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/team-versioning#behavior-with-team-versioning-enabled)

**📦 Behavior With Team Versioning Enabled**

With Team Versioning enabled, Hivel utilizes **historical team structures** to calculate metrics. This ensures each metric reflects which authors were part of a team **at the time the work occurred**.

*   Historical data is preserved.
    
*   Visibility is filtered by the selected date range.
    
*   Contributions remain visible for the period when the member was active.
    
*   No new data for a team is shown after the member’s exit date from the team.
    

**Example 1:**

*   Author A is in Team B (Jan–Feb), then moved to Team C in March.
    
*   You view metrics for:
    
    *   **Jan 15 – Feb 15**: ✅ Author A's contributions appear in **Team B** metrics.
        
    *   **Mar 15 – Apr 15**: ❌ Author A's contributions do **not** appear in Team B metrics, but are part of Team C instead.
        
    

**Example 2:**

Team members: X, Y, Z

*   X and Y are existing employees.
    
*   Z joined the team on March 20, 2026.
    

Selected date range: February 2026

*   Visible members: X, Y
    

Selected date range: Feb 22 – March 19, 2026

*   Visible members: X, Y
    

Selected date range: Feb 22 – March 20, 2026

*   Visible members: X, Y, Z
    

If Y exits the team on March 20, 2026:

*   Y’s historical contributions remain visible for periods prior to March 20, 2026.
    
*   No new activity from Y is shown from March 21, 2026.
    

**Example 3:**

Assume Teams A and B both had 10 members in January 2026.

*   3 members were removed from Team A effective January 31, 2026.
    
*   3 members were removed from Team B effective February 28, 2026.
    

If **February 2026** was selected and teams are viewed separately:

*   Team A shows **7** total members (the 3 members already left).
    
*   Team B shows **10** total members (removal of 3 members occur at the end of February).
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/team-versioning#metric-calculation-note-duration-sensitivity)

Metric calculation note (duration sensitivity)

*   Weekly metrics are normalized to a 7-day week.
    
*   If a member was active for only part of a week (for example, 2 days) and then left the team or organization, the metric is still divided by 7.
    

As a result, that member’s weekly metric may appear lower than expected when viewed at weekly granularity.

* * *

circle-info

**Please Note:** The feature is based solely on user movement across teams, rather than the actual teams themselves. If a team is removed from Hivel, all the associated versioning data will not be retained.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/team-versioning#summary-and-troubleshooting-checklist)

Summary and troubleshooting checklist

Team Versioning provides:

*   Historically accurate reporting
    
*   Date-aware visibility based on join and exit dates
    
*   More reliable metrics and insights during team changes
    

If a dashboard or metric looks inconsistent, verify:

*   The selected date range
    
*   Members join and exit dates
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/team-versioning#why-use-team-versioning)

**📌 Why Use Team Versioning?**

We recommend using Team Versioning to:

*   Analyze metrics accurately for historical team performance.
    
*   Avoid misleading trends caused by team structure changes.
    
*   Support performance reviews and retrospectives based on actual team dynamics at the time.
    

If you’re unsure whether Team Versioning is enabled or want to enable it, reach out to [\[email protected\]envelope](https://docs.hivel.ai/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#5724222727382523173f3e21323b79363e)
.

[PreviousLabelschevron-left](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/labels)
[NextIntegrationschevron-right](https://docs.hivel.ai/integrations)

Last updated 25 days ago

*   [What is Team Versioning?](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/team-versioning#what-is-team-versioning)
    
*   [Metric calculation note (duration sensitivity)](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/team-versioning#metric-calculation-note-duration-sensitivity)
    
*   [Summary and troubleshooting checklist](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/team-versioning#summary-and-troubleshooting-checklist)

# Team level Hivel Score Calculation | Hivel

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/hivel-score/team-level-hivel-score-calculation#what-is-the-team-level-hivel-score)

What is the Team-Level Hivel Score?

The Team-Level Hivel Score gives you a focused view of how a specific team - and its sub-teams - are performing across Speed, Quality, and Throughput. It uses the same scoring framework as the org level, but scoped to the team you select, letting you drill deeper into performance patterns within your org.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/hivel-score/team-level-hivel-score-calculation#setting-up-your-configuration)

Setting Up Your Configuration

The same configuration used at the org level applies here. If you've already set your bucket weights (Speed, Quality, Throughput totalling 100%), you're all set. Scores are calculated only after configuration is saved and are visible for completed months only.

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252Fl1wX60l3Ft2Nwp7tJJVA%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Ddfbf26a0-e66e-42d5-8582-433c7ead8090&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=24ebb1da&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/hivel-score/team-level-hivel-score-calculation#how-the-team-level-hivel-score-is-calculated)

How the Team-Level Hivel Score is Calculated

The score is built bottom-up - from individual metric scores, to bucket scores, to a final team score.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/hivel-score/team-level-hivel-score-calculation#step-1-metric-scores-0-100-scale)

Step 1: Metric Scores (0–100 scale)

Each metric (e.g., Commits, Review Time) is scored by comparing a sub-team's value against all sub-teams' performance over a **rolling 6-month window**, including the current month. This keeps scores contextual and reflective of recent trends.

To ensure scores aren't skewed by extreme outliers or inactive periods, the following data cleaning is applied before scoring:

*   Values of **0 are excluded** (treated as no activity)
    
*   The **top and bottom 2%** of values are removed
    

The remaining values set the scoring range (min to max). Each sub-team's current month value is then plotted within this range to produce a 0–100 score. Sub-teams with no activity (zero value) score 0, while those at the very top of the range score 100.

**Example - Metric: Commits, Month: January**

Here's how 6 months of Commits data across sub-teams translates into January scores:

Sub-Team

Jan Commits

Score

A

0

0 (no activity)

B

120

36.6

C

89

21.46

D

300

100 (top outlier)

E

72

13.17

F

0

0 (no activity)

After removing zeros and 2% outliers from all 6 months of data, the scoring range is set at **Min = 45, Max = 250**. Each sub-team's January value is scored within this range. Sub-team D's value of 300 falls above the top 2% threshold, so it automatically scores 100.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/hivel-score/team-level-hivel-score-calculation#step-2-bucket-scores)

Step 2: Bucket Scores

Within each bucket, metrics carry predefined weights. A sub-team's bucket score is the weighted average of its individual metric scores.

_Example - Throughput bucket with Commits (60%) and PRs Merged (40%):_ A sub-team scoring 80 on Commits and 70 on PRs Merged would receive a Throughput score of **76**.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/hivel-score/team-level-hivel-score-calculation#step-3-final-team-hivel-score)

Step 3: Final Team Hivel Score

The three bucket scores are combined using your configured weights to produce the final Hivel Score for each sub-team.

_Example - with Speed 30%, Quality 40%, Throughput 30%:_ A sub-team with Speed = 60, Quality = 75, Throughput = 76 would receive a Hivel Score of **70.8**.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/hivel-score/team-level-hivel-score-calculation#what-youll-see-on-the-dashboard)

What You'll See on the Dashboard

The team-level dashboard mirrors the org view, scoped to your selected team:

*   **Hivel Score** for the selected month, with a 6-month trend
    
*   **Score Trend Graph** - how the team's score has moved over the past 6 months
    
*   **Category Breakdown** - Speed, Quality, and Throughput scores with expandable metric detail, including each metric's score, weight, and change vs. the 6-month average
    
*   **Sub-Team Ranking Table** - all sub-teams ranked by score, showing % change vs. 6-month average
    

> If the selected team has no sub-teams, the dashboard will display a "No sub-teams available" message.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/hivel-score/team-level-hivel-score-calculation#a-few-things-to-keep-in-mind)

A Few Things to Keep in Mind

*   Scores use a **rolling 6-month window**, so they naturally adapt as your team's performance evolves
    
*   Sub-teams with **no activity** on a metric receive a score of 0 for that metric
    
*   Scores are only visible for **completed months** - no mid-month previews
    
*   If no data is available, the score will show as **0**
    

* * *

_For questions or help with your configuration, please reach out to our support team._

[PreviousOrg level Hivel Score Calculationchevron-left](https://docs.hivel.ai/using-hivel/hivel-score/org-level-hivel-score-calculation)
[NextMetrics & Definitionschevron-right](https://docs.hivel.ai/metrics-and-definitions)

# How to add or update an user's email id? | Hivel

To do this, go to **Settings** → **Users**.

1.  Search for the user in the search bar.
    
2.  Click on the entry.
    
3.  In the right panel that pops up, click on the pencil icon.
    
4.  Add the mail ID in the field and hit "Save".
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FMAO1vM5V9idnA29moz2y%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D18215426-daaa-438a-a1fb-1a73816f1a86&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=9806c20c&sv=2)

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FSbV78TafYtqpjV114vyE%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Df986be37-08e0-417c-90d4-bb4bc5065e65&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=1d163d07&sv=2)

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252F9iypopdwo2F0AQ7XcMKd%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D13818e11-8a1a-4ee7-b9b7-144962ce1703&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=8201be67&sv=2)

circle-exclamation

**Please note:** You can add a user's email id if it isn't there already, **but you cannot edit an existing email id.**

Please contact [\[email protected\]envelope](https://docs.hivel.ai/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#9eedebeeeef1eceadef6f7e8fbf2b0fff7)
 to change the email id.

# Cursor Adoption | Hivel

circle-info

To integrate Cursor and start seeing the following metrics, see [_**here**_arrow-up-right](https://docs.hivel.ai/integrations/cursor-adoption)
.

Hivel's **Cursor Adoption** feature offers detailed insights into how well the Cursor AI is being utilized within a team or whole organization and how useful it is proving to be.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/ai-adoption/cursor-adoption#overview)

Overview

**User Coverage Graph**

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FeWeSueBOmhwIKBCwjm4T%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D82584890-45e4-4d30-86d3-b44f82bb7df2&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c22c375&sv=2)

*   This graph shows the trend of **active** and **inactive** users over different time periods (weekly, monthly, quarterly).
    
*   It provides a high-level overview of Cursor adoption across teams and helps identify periods of higher or lower engagement.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/ai-adoption/cursor-adoption#suggestions-acceptance-rate)

**Suggestions Acceptance Rate**

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FUemcxknXj8JNC9y4wBRb%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D6e5de83d-6c7f-43c4-98ba-6488625cdfed&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=ec54c7fc&sv=2)

*   This metric shows how useful users find Cursor’s suggestions. A higher acceptance rate indicates that users are finding the suggestions useful enough to directly accept them.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/ai-adoption/cursor-adoption#ai-vs-manual-code)

**AI vs Manual Code**

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FnU98webcdwUt5aJfxrAS%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D68e21bba-a7c1-4da2-9b1f-b58e1e93e1be&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=7e69b4d0&sv=2)

*   This graph helps you understand the volume of **AI-generated code** versus manually written code in your codebase.
    
*   Even if the suggestions acceptance rate is high, this graph reveals whether users are integrating Cursor deeply into their workflow or just using it occasionally.
    
*   A lower percentage of AI-generated code indicates that users might be using Cursor as an afterthought rather than as a central part of their workflow.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/ai-adoption/cursor-adoption#ai-models-and-extensions)

**AI Models and Extensions**

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252F4bLARxCyG7vlhvCmdJEp%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D03ccefc7-2874-402e-9b20-32662c16caab&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=482ce44f&sv=2)

*   These charts show:
    
    *   **AI Models**: Usage across different AI models in Cursor.
        
    *   **Extensions**: Visualizes AI-generated code by programming languages
        
    
*   **Note**: Both charts exclude tab completions, focusing only on the core usage.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/ai-adoption/cursor-adoption#a-few-high-level-usage-metrics)

A few high-level usage metrics

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252Flrb1RM1rvjdYga060mfM%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D067e12d1-4f5c-4d51-9226-a42de7acb5ab&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=7cd8d52&sv=2)

**Total Paid Seats**:

*   This represents the number of licensed users in the current subscription cycle.
    
*   It is not tied to specific dates or teams, just the total number of users for the subscription.
    

**Active Users**:

*   Active users are those who have engaged with Cursor during the selected time frame. Activities include logging in, accepting suggestions, writing code, or making requests.
    

**Inactive Users**:

*   Inactive users are those who have not performed any actions within the selected time frame.
    

circle-info

The Active + Inactive count may differ from the Total Paid Seats because it is based on the selected timeframe and teams, which may not always match the total license count.

**Total Bubot Calls**:

*   This counts the number of times **Bugbot** (Cursor's code review tool) has been used during the selected time frame.
    

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/ai-adoption/cursor-adoption#ai-usage-analysis)

**AI Usage Analysis**

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FhYPRl97QvwIxEu3C2mTO%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D2e4a9a4c-d956-439a-94d4-69041008ec11&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=c0c13a73&sv=2)

The **AI Usage Analysis** tab breaks down individual user activity, showing:

*   The total lines of code each user has written.
    
*   The percentage of code that was AI-generated versus manually written.
    

**Cohorts for AI Usage**

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FVslwguXZPxOP1wA6Erkr%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D19c92e52-f424-4d0e-a825-a00a8ccde619&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=2314e8d6&sv=2)

*   **High Usage (>=70%)**: These are the top users who rely heavily on AI to assist in coding.
    
*   **Medium Usage (30-69%)**: These users make moderate use of AI in their coding.
    
*   **Low Usage (<30%)**: These users are minimally relying on AI.
    

This segmentation is helpful for identifying your AI "trailblazers" (those with high usage) who can share best practices and tips with others who have low usage. By fostering collaboration between cohorts, your organization can maximize the value gained from Cursor.

* * *

By tracking these metrics and visualizations, you can gain valuable insights into how teams are using Cursor, who is benefiting most from its features, and where there may be opportunities to encourage greater adoption or improve workflow integration.

[PreviousGitHub Copilot: Expanded Metrics Guidechevron-left](https://docs.hivel.ai/ai-adoption/copilot-adoption/github-copilot-expanded-metrics-guide)
[NextCursor: Expanded Metrics Guidechevron-right](https://docs.hivel.ai/ai-adoption/cursor-adoption/cursor-expanded-metrics-guide)

Last updated 8 months ago

*   [Overview](https://docs.hivel.ai/ai-adoption/cursor-adoption#overview)
    
*   [AI Usage Analysis](https://docs.hivel.ai/ai-adoption/cursor-adoption#ai-usage-analysis)

# How to merge users? | Hivel

Sometimes, while importing users from Git, there may be a duplication of users because developers commit using their personal email ids or use the same personal access token on a different machine. In such cases you can merge multiple users into one primary user.

circle-info

Please note: **This action cannot be undone.** If you have mistakenly merged users together please contact [\[email protected\]envelope](https://docs.hivel.ai/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#72010702021d0006321a1b04171e5c131b)
 for assistance.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/users/how-to-merge-users#here-is-how-to-merge-users-in-hivel)

Here is how to merge users in Hivel:

1\. Go to **Settings** **→** **Users**

2\. Select the users you want to merge

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252Foik2F8twIp8BFINx56o0%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dd0de3a0a-95d5-46d9-8198-310e04cac635&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=1c076c56&sv=2)

3\. Click on the **Merge** icon.

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FyfqYZ4JmY9Clhx1nID0E%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D83fab3ab-e6e2-41ab-9de1-0dfc5ceb3ef9&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=a3dfdfd4&sv=2)

4\. Select a primary user

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FN95u6NJvRWxLflTbB1iq%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D7a364a6a-3552-42ee-9c52-07c89e783e2e&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=668a2cba&sv=2)

5\. Click **Merge**

[PreviousHow to add or update an user's email id?chevron-left](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/users/how-to-add-or-update-an-users-email-id)
[NextHow to update the name of an user?chevron-right](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/users/how-to-update-the-name-of-an-user)

# Can I see the data of a user or repo that I don’t have access to on my SCM tool? | Hivel

No, you can not access any users or repositories on Hivel if you don’t have access to them on the SCM tool.

# How to create teams? | Hivel

*   Go to **Settings** → **Teams** → **Create Team**
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FeXp0igiuOWQRxm9eUzuQ%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D0a536ccb-944a-4bd3-b800-c9055fe18265&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=785ecc71&sv=2)

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252F7D2VdjKUA04HJ2HLIPyq%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D726db11b-103d-441c-87ef-d1a7b8319338&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=e89b5e04&sv=2)

*   Enter a team name and select a team owner. Don't worry, you can always change these later if needed.
    
*   Click **Create and add**. You can add additional members in the next step if required.
    
*   A single team member can be added to multiple teams. This way, you can classify an engineer into their squads, engineers by seniority, location, etc.

# Access Management | Hivel

The Access Management system provides a more structured, secure, and flexible approach to access. This ensures that the right individuals have appropriate control based on their responsibilities.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/access-management#access-management-role-hierarchy)

**Access Management Role Hierarchy**

To establish clear permissions and responsibilities, we have introduced **five distinct roles**:

1.  **Admin** _(Full access to the entire platform, responsible for managing permissions and settings)_
    
2.  **Executive** _(CXOs level i.e. CTO, CEO and Founders)_
    
3.  **Leader** _(VPs, Director and Department heads)_
    
4.  **Managers** _(Team Leads, Engineering Managers and Project Managers)_
    
5.  **User** _(Individual contributors like developers)_
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252Fm0pHxOMKZs9j3SrDxemn%252F1st%2520Img.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D1a3fa1dd-0f76-4221-baba-62cdcf046486&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=9735c0cc&sv=2)

Each role is assigned specific permissions, ensuring a well-defined access structure and preventing unauthorized modifications.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/access-management#am-screen-structure-and-functionality)

**AM Screen: Structure & Functionality**

The **RBAC screen** is divided into three dedicated tabs:

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/access-management#id-1.-role-access-only-admins-can-access)

**1\. Role Access (only Admins can access)**

This tab provides **Admins** with full control over roles and permissions. Key functionalities include:

*   **Viewing assigned permissions** for each role.
    
*   **Modifying role permissions** as needed.
    
*   **Saving changes** for real-time updates.
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FFrtxA03AIBSafrt9tlkq%252F2n%2520Img.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D9193caa3-a49d-4dca-a944-9c03701b5826&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=a986b7d4&sv=2)

This centralized approach ensures permissions are **accurately assigned** while maintaining security and flexibility.

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/access-management#id-2.-user-management)

**2\. User Management**

This section allows for efficient user administration by displaying a **list of users** in the system.

**Note:** If multiple users are merged in the **Teams** screen, only the **Primary User** will be displayed in this tab.

**Key functionalities:**

*   **Inviting new users:**
    
    *   If a person is not yet a user, they can be invited via the **"Invite"** button in the last column.
        
    *   Clicking this button allows Admins to:
        
        *   **Select the user role**
            
        *   **Assign them to teams, projects, and workspaces** (if enabled)
            
        
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FywwBiJfyWqYBmeDrtWjc%252F3rd%2520Img%2520-%2520New.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D82a61641-29d1-4280-b42e-07e000c881b2&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=a9a6a237&sv=2)

*   **Editing existing users:**
    
    *   Modify a user’s **role, team, projects, and workspaces** (if enabled).
        
    *   Users **cannot** modify their own details or the role of anyone **above them** in the hierarchy.
        
    *   Users **can only edit roles at their level or below**, ensuring secure delegation.
        
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252F7mhfSpvHyMUxSuGflWIa%252F4th%2520Img.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D174e4154-e69c-4b0f-9751-57d588d0ac44&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=f88293d2&sv=2)

_Adjust roles_

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FkkTXjTvOPdM8UXIla3Zs%252F5th%2520img%2520%281%29.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dea29ba55-3c9c-4025-9bbf-eefa76b77bac&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=8f3f95c2&sv=2)

_Select teams which can be accessed_

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FawoMl6A9e1pXQaaCdA6g%252F6th%2520Img%2520-%2520new.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D71906631-c53a-41c3-bea8-f16c7a35a6d5&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=6988e16&sv=2)

_Select projects which can be accesed_

* * *

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/access-management#id-3.-pending-access-requests-admin-only)

**3\. Pending Access Requests (Admin-Only)**

For organizations that require **Admin approval** for new user sign-ups, this tab acts as a **centralized approval hub**.

**How it works:**

*   When a new user requests access, the **Admin receives an email notification**.
    
*   All **pending access requests** appear in this section.
    
*   The Admin can then **approve or deny** requests, ensuring controlled onboarding.
    
    ![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FqB4103Hm0ekdiVhj8ZNH%252F7th%2520Img.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D376a3055-43db-414f-a202-eca5d7759e8d&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=710eeccd&sv=2)

# Labels | Hivel

**Labels** in Hivel allow you to tag users with additional metadata that you can later use to filter across various metrics and reporting screens. They’re highly flexible and customizable, helping you organize users beyond just teams or roles.

circle-info

Please note: Labels will be set at an org level and be visible to everyone as filters.

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/labels#what-you-can-do-with-labels)

What You Can Do with Labels

*   Add meaningful tags to users (e.g. `Location: APAC`, `Seniority: Senior`, `Department: Frontend`)
    
*   Assign multiple labels to one or more users
    
*   Group labels into **categories** for better organization
    
*   Filter metrics and insights using these labels
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252Fix5oVVEfTgkKP9bRVKTG%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dbd095860-c442-422b-9b9d-186b27bed4ce&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=4dc1c114&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/labels#how-to-set-up-labels)

🛠️ How to Set Up Labels

1.  **Go to the Labels Screen**
    
    *   Navigate to **Settings → Labels**.
        
    
2.  **Create a Category (if needed)**
    
    *   All labels must belong to a **category**.
        
    *   Click **"Add Category"** if you don’t already have one.
        
    
3.  **Add a New Label**
    
    *   Under an existing category, click **“Add Label”**.
        
    *   Enter the label name (e.g. `Contractor`, `Europe`, `Level 2`).
        
    
    > **Note:** Labels **must belong to a category** - they cannot exist independently.
    
    *   ![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252Flu8PAUk74DYN4oQIDlXs%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D972ed58a-4447-4ccd-8142-932f4cb3864a&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=d75be54c&sv=2)
        
    
4.  **Edit or Remove Labels and Categories**
    
    *   Click the ✏️ (pencil) icon to **edit**.
        
    *   Click the ❌ (cross) icon to **delete**.
        
    *   **Deleting a label** will remove it from **all users** it's currently assigned to.
        
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FeCVKdTPNZRO0NZuXrMkS%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Da95d2564-b866-4cc1-a382-f13e86631212&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=cd51eb75&sv=2)

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FCS6x98vhoarfBMMCT48O%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dfbe3c3ff-5d5c-4df6-b662-5a0c986bbb71&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=44593820&sv=2)

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/labels#assign-labels-to-users)

👥 Assign Labels to Users

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252F8003OMaH35Dvr5yDvzRW%252FScreenshot%25202025-09-15%2520at%25202.20.00%25E2%2580%25AFPM.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dab1f6228-b489-47fb-8734-824670a33941&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=eb4cafcc&sv=2)

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252Fz3DpbZkWOzcCrdLKSShT%252FScreenshot%25202025-09-15%2520at%25202.20.27%25E2%2580%25AFPM.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Df9d13dbb-afcd-40ab-aed1-c2bf0d172624&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=be23014b&sv=2)

1.  Go to the **Users** screen.
    
2.  Select one or multiple users.
    
3.  Click the **Labels icon**.
    
4.  Choose the labels to assign and click **Save**.
    

* * *

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/labels#filtering-by-labels)

🔎 Filtering by Labels

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FoUzIchWORu3C4OhBcemA%252FScreen%2520Cast%25202025-09-15%2520at%25201.59.49%2520PM.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Db9c75130-4af9-4cbf-aac6-71799cff7ecd&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=4722778d&sv=2)

Once labels are assigned:

*   You’ll see **label filters** across Hivel’s metrics and reporting screens.
    
*   These filters act as an **extra layer of user segmentation**, making it easier to analyze specific cohorts.
    

* * *

# How to invite more users to use Hivel? | Hivel

If the user does not have a Git account, they can sign up using [app.hivel.ai/signuparrow-up-right](http://app.hivel.ai/signup)

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/users/how-to-invite-more-users-to-use-hivel#if-the-user-has-a-git-account-then-follow-the-below-steps)

**If the user has a Git account then follow the below steps -**

1.  Go to **Settings.**
    
2.  Select [Access Management](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/access-management)
    
3.  Click on User Management.
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252F70pHuv2tBd2DYCDIRjLQ%252FScreenshot%25202025-02-20%2520at%25205.16.25%2520PM.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D0c426088-3ee4-410f-9bd8-3a77491d0fbc&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=f339efe6&sv=2)

4\. Search for the user in the user list or use the search tab.

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FvEUTMTWHVWx3uSJEZam0%252FScreenshot%25202025-02-20%2520at%25206.00.35%2520PM.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dc2881577-7d4b-44ee-9bd1-89a3a65915c2&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=f429c434&sv=2)

5\. Click on the Invite option for new users.

6\. If the user has no email ID associated with their name, manually enter the email address.

7\. Select the role based on the hierarchy.

*   **Admin** _(Full access to the entire platform, responsible for managing permissions and settings)_
    
*   **Executive** _(CTO, CEO and Founders)_
    
*   **Leader** _(VPs, Director and Department heads)_
    
*   **Managers** _(Team Leads, Engineering Managers and Project Managers)_
    
*   **User** _(Developers and Engineers)_
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FwBJERbPHXSE0WFdIUOG4%252FScreenshot%25202025-02-20%2520at%25205.13.57%2520PM.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D1fed3a30-15fd-4457-92d3-ec044bd294c4&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=d4e513d7&sv=2)

circle-info

**Click on Continue at every step to save the progress.**

1.  Assign the user to relevant teams and projects.
    
2.  An email invite will automatically be sent to the user.
    

If you encounter any issues, contact [\[email protected\]envelope](https://docs.hivel.ai/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#c5b6b0b5b5aab7b185adacb3a0a9eba4ac)
 for assistance.

[PreviousUserschevron-left](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/users)
[NextHow to add or update an user's email id?chevron-right](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/users/how-to-add-or-update-an-users-email-id)

Last updated 3 months ago

# How to delete a team? | Hivel

You can only delete teams that _you_ have created. To delete a team -

1.  Go to **Settings** → **Team**
    
2.  Select a team -> then 3 dots on the right.
    
3.  Click the delete icon.
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252F9LuZaHokJ5l5r2b01v9T%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D3c8a3c2f-637d-437d-8245-ed7093bb369c&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=f6628c06&sv=2)

# How to create sub-teams? | Hivel

The best way to view data in Hivel is by team. If you have a sub-team structure at your company, Hivel's got you covered too.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/teams/how-to-create-sub-teams#here-is-how-to-create-sub-teams-in-hivel)

Here is how to create sub-teams in Hivel:

1\. Go to **Settings →Teams**

2\. If you don't have any teams created yet, [create a team](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/teams/how-to-create-teams)

3\. Select the team within which you want to create a sub-team

4\. Navigate to Subteam menu using the toggle.

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252Fu4pj5fXghPTRKEps0Ro2%252FScreenshot%25202025-11-11%2520at%252012.13.27%25E2%2580%25AFPM.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Df962c67d-7a01-4e8b-8c71-6f8ffcf61739&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=34ad1936&sv=2)

5\. Select 'Create Subteam' and in the dialog box enter team name select a **team owner**, followed by adding other users.

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FeJGXyQBTEZ20CJSNNFr2%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Df47267d0-aaa0-414d-8ef3-47a440babecf&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=9f19befe&sv=2)

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252F3D1QEKSn5FQtyCRBJIig%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Da2d6d211-2a96-473e-b91f-fcf65dea60b5&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=5913c68&sv=2)

6\. Click **Create Subteam.**

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FxqNDLPNOt6vC6UZ6Egk3%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D862c5dfa-fc5f-478b-8d2d-395b381e917f&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=95fc4235&sv=2)

7\. You can view your sub-teams within the main team succesfully.

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FA36rOvffU3NZ6UD7t8Up%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D2cb55d31-087e-41a0-a675-29552a08e56c&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=321017bb&sv=2)

> If the changes are not reflected immediately, refresh the the screen to reflect the changes.

[NextHow to add users to a team and sub-team?chevron-right](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/teams/how-to-add-users-to-a-team-and-sub-team)

# Marco - Code Review Tool | Hivel

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/integrations/marco-code-review-tool#getting-started-with-hivel-code-review)

Getting Started with Hivel Code Review

Welcome to your new AI-powered code review companion. This guide will help you configure your environment and understand how to get the most out of hivel-marco, our intelligent review agent.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/integrations/marco-code-review-tool#configuration-and-setup)

⚙️ Configuration & Setup

Control how the AI interacts with your code through the Hivel dashboard.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/integrations/marco-code-review-tool#id-1.-organizational-settings)

1\. Organizational Settings

Admins can manage review behavior by navigating to:

👉 [app.hivel.ai/settings/code-reviewarrow-up-right](https://app.hivel.ai/settings/code-review)

In this section, you can define:

*   Specific Instructions: Custom guidelines the AI should follow (e.g., "Ensure all functions have JSDoc").
    
*   Global Filters: Files or directories to include or exclude across all projects.
    
*   Default Branches: Set the standard target branches for reviews across your organization.
    

Note: These settings serve as your "baseline" but can be overridden at the individual repository level for maximum flexibility.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/integrations/marco-code-review-tool#id-2.-repository-level-configs)

2\. Repository Level Configs

For the highest quality reviews, we recommend indexing your repository when enabling them for the first time. While Marco will still review PRs without this step, indexing allows the AI to understand your entire codebase contextually.

*   Analyze/Reanalyze: Trigger a manual scan of your repo to update the AI’s mental model of your project.
    

Note: We recommend reanalyzing your repo at the end of each sprint or when a sizable revamp/ feature is added to it. A repository owner can make the final decision of what they consider to be a sizable change.

*   Override Configs: Any of the org-level configs such as instructions, file filters and branches can also be configured here, at the repo level. Any modifications at the repo stage, override the Org Level configs.
    

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/integrations/marco-code-review-tool#working-in-github)

🚀 Working in GitHub

Once enabled, the review process is entirely automated. Look for the hivel-marco bot in your Pull Requests.

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/integrations/marco-code-review-tool#automated-triggers)

Automated Triggers

*   New PRs: When a PR is raised against a configured target branch, a review is automatically triggered.
    
*   Incremental Updates: If you push new code to an existing open PR, Marco performs an incremental review. It only analyzes the new changes to avoid repeating previous suggestions.
    

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/integrations/marco-code-review-tool#the-review-report)

The Review Report

Every review includes three core components:

Feature

Description

Security Check

First Priority: We scan for Secrets or PII. These are sanitized before reaching the AI to keep your data safe. If detected, remove them before merging!

PR Summary

A concise overview of what the PR intends to accomplish.

File Breakdown

A contextual map of changes, categorized by file.

Complexity Score

An intelligent estimate of the review effort required (see below).

**Understanding Complexity Scores**

We look beyond "Lines of Code" to calculate how difficult a PR is to digest:

Score

Description

1.0 – 2.0

Minor tweaks, typos, or simple config updates.

2.1 – 4.0

Straightforward logic changes or small features.

4.1 – 6.0

Standard feature work or moderate refactoring.

6.1 – 8.0

Significant logic changes; requires deep focus.

8.1 – 10.0

High-risk architectural changes or massive diffs.

### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/integrations/marco-code-review-tool#actionable-suggestions)

🛠️ Actionable Suggestions

Marco doesn't just critique; it provides solutions. Suggestions are posted directly on the relevant lines of code within the GitHub UI.

*   Criticality Levels: Suggestions are tagged as Low, Medium, High, or Critical to help you prioritize fixes.
    
*   Explanations: Each suggestion includes why the change is needed and how to implement the fix.
    
*   One-Click Fixes: You can accept suggestions directly within GitHub.
    
*   Pro Tip: Use the "Batch Suggestions" feature in GitHub’s "Files Changed" tab to review and commit multiple AI suggestions in a single go.
    

Disclaimer: While our AI agent is highly advanced, it may occasionally make mistakes. Always re-test your code after committing AI-suggested changes.

[PreviousIntegrationschevron-left](https://docs.hivel.ai/integrations)
[NextSCMchevron-right](https://docs.hivel.ai/integrations/scm)

Last updated 1 month ago

*   [⚙️ Configuration & Setup](https://docs.hivel.ai/integrations/marco-code-review-tool#configuration-and-setup)

# How to remove users from a team or sub-team? | Hivel

To **remove users from a team or sub-team** in Hivel, follow these steps:

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/teams/how-to-remove-users-from-a-team-or-sub-team#steps-to-remove-users)

Steps to Remove Users:

1.  **Navigate to the Teams page**: Go to the Teams page and select the particular team from which you want to remove users.
    
2.  **Select the Users to Remove**: Find and select all the users that you wish to remove from the team.
    
3.  **Click on the "Delete" Icon**: On the right corner of the user selection list, click on the **"Delete"** icon to remove the users from the team.
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FoIqwnbxdyNXex2ZTqjJS%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D87ffc968-804f-4749-b961-90077b7e94a3&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=172601ff&sv=2)

circle-info

**Important**: If you **remove a user from the parent team**, they will also be removed from **all sub-teams** under that parent team.

If a user is **only removed from a sub-team**, they will **remain part of the parent team**. This is by design, as a user can be part of the larger parent team even if not part of its sub-teams.

circle-info

**Another Note**: Removing users from a team does not delete their data. If the user becomes part of another team later, their data will still be available and visible when that new team is selected.

To permanently remove an user from the platform, use the [archive functionality](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/users/how-to-archive-users)
.

[PreviousHow to add users to a team and sub-team?chevron-left](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/teams/how-to-add-users-to-a-team-and-sub-team)
[NextAccess Managementchevron-right](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/access-management)

Last updated 1 month ago

# How to add users to a team and sub-team? | Hivel

To add authors to a team on the Teams page in Hivel, you can follow these methods:

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/teams/how-to-add-users-to-a-team-and-sub-team#id-1.-if-the-team-is-already-created)

1\. **If the Team is Already Created:**

*   Navigate to the **Teams** page and select the specific team you want to add authors to.
    
*   Once inside the team, click on the **"Add Users"** button.
    
*   In the search bar, type the name of the users you want to add, and select the applicable users from the list.
    
*   The selected users will be added as an author to the team.
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252FBbFhYsssL8LNHCJN1ESd%252FScreen%2520Cast%25202026-01-30%2520at%25201.03.29%2520PM.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dbed85b0b-8673-4d35-b374-1b1d2d50fcc5&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=2b3ffe1b&sv=2)

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/teams/how-to-add-users-to-a-team-and-sub-team#id-2.-if-the-team-is-not-created)

2\. **If the Team is Not Created:**

*   Select all the users who should be part of the team.
    
*   Click on the **"Create Team"** button.
    
*   Fill in the required details about the team, such as the team name, description, and any other relevant information.
    
*   After filling in the details, save the team. The selected users will be added as authors automatically.
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252F4hCFqk8ZN6HMMXr1QGeT%252FScreen%2520Cast%25202026-01-30%2520at%25201.06.45%2520PM.gif%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3Dc03e59e3-3498-4901-aea6-b471892c49c0&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=af0dbe83&sv=2)

#### 

[hashtag](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/teams/how-to-add-users-to-a-team-and-sub-team#id-3.-to-add-users-to-a-sub-team)

3\. **To add users to a sub-team**

*   You can navigate directly to the subteam by expanding the parent team.
    
    ![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252F92y06K5ucvD2ALikdHL9%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D37f083b3-a667-4742-b463-dc36f1db2409&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=811acdc0&sv=2)
    
*   Or you can, navigate to the parent team -> then switch to Subteams section -> Select the subteam.
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252F2LZimVlxDo1wZZJHx5zu%252Fimage.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D9eac139b-02b8-4ece-9b41-ae797602d7a3&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=382a679&sv=2)

*   Once inside the subteam, click on "Add Users" and select all the users who should be part of the subteam.
    

![](https://docs.hivel.ai/~gitbook/image?url=https%3A%2F%2F3057781534-files.gitbook.io%2F%7E%2Ffiles%2Fv0%2Fb%2Fgitbook-x-prod.appspot.com%2Fo%2Fspaces%252F5KAIOUWph0JLSgQqbzyT%252Fuploads%252F1JB7KZX0Sa2VKCC2vAyn%252FScreenshot%25202026-01-30%2520at%25201.18.26%25E2%2580%25AFPM.png%3Falt%3Dmedia%26token%3D838cbd19-1a36-4bcc-abce-93963c66b188&width=768&dpr=3&quality=100&sign=bfb9b6d3&sv=2)

*   After filling in the details, save the team. The selected users will be added as authors automatically.
    

By following these steps, you'll be able to effectively add authors to a team or sub-teams, whether it's already created or not.

[PreviousHow to create sub-teams?chevron-left](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/teams/how-to-create-sub-teams)
[NextHow to remove users from a team or sub-team?chevron-right](https://docs.hivel.ai/set-up/teams/how-to-remove-users-from-a-team-or-sub-team)
